Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

I. VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<span class="line"><!---->I. VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It is possible to trigger a callback during the computation of IterateElements used by Array.concat(). This is done by controlling the return type of Array.concat() (visitor variable) by setting the Symbol.species of the receiving element to the function. In this example we set TypedArray. When properties are set on our receiver during the IterateElements instruction the JSReceiver::CreateDataProperty [1] is called which doesn't trigger any getters or setters directly on our object due to the checks put in place after 681761 (CVE-2017-5030). However it is possible to trigger a callback because the codepath JSObject::CreateElement leads to a call Object::ToNumber when TypedArray's are passed as an argument [2]. Once these are bypassed the array can be shrunk and moved to old space leading to OOB read for infoleak and fakeobj for full RCE [3]



<span class="line"><!---->It is possible to trigger a callback during the computation of IterateElements used by Array.concat(). This is done by controlling the return type of Array.concat() (visitor variable) by setting the Symbol.species of the receiving element to the function. In this example we set TypedArray. When properties are set on our receiver during the IterateElements instruction the JSReceiver::CreateDataProperty [1] is called which doesn't trigger any getters or setters directly on our object due to the checks put in place after 681761 (CVE-2017-5030). However it is possible to trigger a callback because the codepath JSObject::CreateElement leads to a call Object::ToNumber when TypedArray's are passed as an argument [2]. Once these are bypassed the array can be shrunk and moved to old space leading to OOB read for infoleak and fakeobj for full RCE [3]<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[1] 



<span class="line"><!---->[1] <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:v8/src/builtins/builtins-array.cc;l=1097;drc=3f9ff062b053155df7897f199e80a8bafe7c34df



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:v8/src/builtins/builtins-array.cc;l=1097;drc=3f9ff062b053155df7897f199e80a8bafe7c34df"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:v8/src/builtins/builtins-array.cc;l=1097;drc=3f9ff062b053155df7897f199e80a8bafe7c34df<!----></a>



<br>





[2] 



<span class="line"><!---->[2] <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:v8/src/objects/objects.cc;l=2805;drc=9ba6750ad3912c31b2c411cb309f724293859c41



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:v8/src/objects/objects.cc;l=2805;drc=9ba6750ad3912c31b2c411cb309f724293859c41"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:v8/src/objects/objects.cc;l=2805;drc=9ba6750ad3912c31b2c411cb309f724293859c41<!----></a>

<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:v8/src/builtins/builtins-array.cc;l=1095;drc=3f9ff062b053155df7897f199e80a8bafe7c34df"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:v8/src/builtins/builtins-array.cc;l=1095;drc=3f9ff062b053155df7897f199e80a8bafe7c34df<!----></a>

II. REPRODUCTION CASE



<span class="line"><!---->II. REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>





class Leaky extends Float64Array {}



<span class="line"><!---->class Leaky extends Float64Array {}<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





let u32 = new Leaky (1000);



<span class="line"><!---->let u32 = new Leaky (1000);<!----></span>



<br>





u32.__defineSetter__('length', function() {});



<span class="line"><!---->u32.__defineSetter__('length', function() {});<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





class MyArray extends Array {



<span class="line"><!---->class MyArray extends Array {<!----></span>



<br>





    static get [Symbol.species]() {



<span class="line"><!---->    static get [Symbol.species]() {<!----></span>



<br>





        return function() { return u32; }



<span class="line"><!---->        return function() { return u32; }<!----></span>



<br>





    };



<span class="line"><!---->    };<!----></span>



<br>





}

Attached is an exploit for the renderer process.



<span class="line"><!---->Attached is an exploit for the renderer process.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Steps to reproduce



<span class="line"><!---->Steps to reproduce<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. Install google chrome stable (89.0.4389.114)



<span class="line"><!---->1. Install google chrome stable (89.0.4389.114)<!----></span>



<br>





2. Run google chrome stable with the --no-sandbox flag



<span class="line"><!---->2. Run google chrome stable with the --no-sandbox flag<!----></span>



<br>





3. Host exploit.html and exploit.js with an html server. I use python -m SimpleHTTPServer 8080



<span class="line"><!---->3. Host exploit.html and exploit.js with an html server. I use python -m SimpleHTTPServer 8080<!----></span>



<br>





4. Navigate to exploit.html. google-chrome --no-sandbox 



<span class="line"><!---->4. Navigate to exploit.html. google-chrome --no-sandbox <!----></span>





http://localhost:8080/exploit.html



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://localhost:8080/exploit.html"><!---->http://localhost:8080/exploit.html<!----></a>



<br>





5. Check the /tmp directory for a new file `aaa` which contains the contents of /etc/passwd



<span class="line"><!---->5. Check the /tmp directory for a new file `aaa` which contains the contents of /etc/passwd<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





or



<span class="line"><!---->or<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. fetch chromium && cd src



<span class="line"><!---->1. fetch chromium &amp;&amp; cd src<!----></span>



<br>





2. git --reset hard 89.0.4389.114



<span class="line"><!---->2. git --reset hard 89.0.4389.114<!----></span>



<br>





3. build release



<span class="line"><!---->3. build release<!----></span>



<br>





4. Host exploit.html and exploit.js with an html server. I use python -m SimpleHTTPServer 8080



<span class="line"><!---->4. Host exploit.html and exploit.js with an html server. I use python -m SimpleHTTPServer 8080<!----></span>



<br>





5. ./out/x64.release/out --no-sandbox 



<span class="line"><!---->5. ./out/x64.release/out --no-sandbox <!----></span>





http://localhost:8080/exploit.html



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://localhost:8080/exploit.html"><!---->http://localhost:8080/exploit.html<!----></a>



<br>





6. Check the /tmp directory for a new file `aaa` which contains the contents of /etc/passwd



<span class="line"><!---->6. Check the /tmp directory for a new file `aaa` which contains the contents of /etc/passwd<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Tested on Ubuntu 18.04 Linux 5.4.0-70-generic x86_64



<span class="line"><!---->Tested on Ubuntu 18.04 Linux 5.4.0-70-generic x86_64<!----></span>

btiszka@ thanks for the report, and thanks for 



<span class="line"><!---->btiszka@ thanks for the report, and thanks for <!----></span>





#c14



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c14"><!---->#c14<!----></a>





. n-day attacks remain a persistent problem. We don't have any systematized method to make fixes in private branches -- it can be done, but it tends to prevent any of our normal QA processes from happening (which is why we don't do it as a matter of course). If the V8 team can temporarily avoid checking in the regression test, that'd be great, but I'll leave it to their judgement to weigh up the security vs stability risks. Meanwhile though we are now better at pushing out fixes sooner, as we now have bi-weekly regular releases and we'll aim to ship the fix here in the next available such release after the fix lands.



<span class="line"><!---->. n-day attacks remain a persistent problem. We don't have any systematized method to make fixes in private branches -- it can be done, but it tends to prevent any of our normal QA processes from happening (which is why we don't do it as a matter of course). If the V8 team can temporarily avoid checking in the regression test, that'd be great, but I'll leave it to their judgement to weigh up the security vs stability risks. Meanwhile though we are now better at pushing out fixes sooner, as we now have bi-weekly regular releases and we'll aim to ship the fix here in the next available such release after the fix lands.<!----></span>

I uploaded a second patch that hardens this codepath. This patch will prevent any variants of this vulnerability from happening again in the future. There have been a total of four vulnerabilities following this pattern in this code path 386988, 594574, 682194, and now 1195977. This patch will also remove an excellent exploitation primitive I found that can be used to "amplify" worse vulnerabilities that aren't easy to exploit.



<span class="line"><!---->I uploaded a second patch that hardens this codepath. This patch will prevent any variants of this vulnerability from happening again in the future. There have been a total of four vulnerabilities following this pattern in this code path 386988, 594574, 682194, and now 1195977. This patch will also remove an excellent exploitation primitive I found that can be used to "amplify" worse vulnerabilities that aren't easy to exploit.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The exploitation primitive works as follows:



<span class="line"><!---->The exploitation primitive works as follows:<!----></span>



<br>





1. Find a vulnerability that results in an OOB write or type confusion that is difficult to exploit.



<span class="line"><!---->1. Find a vulnerability that results in an OOB write or type confusion that is difficult to exploit.<!----></span>



<br>





2. Overwrite the "require_slow_elements()" bit of a Dictionary object.



<span class="line"><!---->2. Overwrite the "require_slow_elements()" bit of a Dictionary object.<!----></span>



<br>





3. Javascript execution in the middle of IterateElements is now possible because our corrupted object passes this check [1] because this [2] returns false.



<span class="line"><!---->3. Javascript execution in the middle of IterateElements is now possible because our corrupted object passes this check [1] because this [2] returns false.<!----></span>



<br>





4. Exploit using the same technique shown above.



<span class="line"><!---->4. Exploit using the same technique shown above.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Patch Explanation



<span class="line"><!---->Patch Explanation<!----></span>



<br>





-----



<span class="line"><!---->-----<!----></span>



<br>





If javascirpt is ever executed after this check [3] it can be used to cause memory corruption. I have added `DisallowJavascirptExecution` to those scopes which crashes with a `CHECK` if javascript is ever executed in the `HasElement`, `GetElement`, or `CreateDataProperty` calls. The `if` statement in `IterateElements` [3] should prevent JavaScript from ever executing in normal situations, but this patch prevents anything like this from slipping through the cracks again.



<span class="line"><!---->If javascirpt is ever executed after this check [3] it can be used to cause memory corruption. I have added `DisallowJavascirptExecution` to those scopes which crashes with a `CHECK` if javascript is ever executed in the `HasElement`, `GetElement`, or `CreateDataProperty` calls. The `if` statement in `IterateElements` [3] should prevent JavaScript from ever executing in normal situations, but this patch prevents anything like this from slipping through the cracks again.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:v8/src/builtins/builtins-array.cc;l=1076;drc=7989e04979c3195e60a6814e8263063eb91f7b47"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:v8/src/builtins/builtins-array.cc;l=1076;drc=7989e04979c3195e60a6814e8263063eb91f7b47<!----></a>



<br>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

        /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM
         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }
